Drop rows where target is NaN\n    64→            valid_idx = y.notna()\n    65→            if not valid_idx.any():\n    66→                print(f\"    WARNING: all targets NaN; skipping\", flush=True)\n    67→                continue\n    68→            X = X[valid_idx]\n    69→            y = y[valid_idx]\n    70→\n    71→            print(f\"    Feature count: {len(feature_cols)}, training samples: {len(X)}\", flush=True)\n    72→\n    73→            # Quick training: fit all models\n    82→            print(f\"    Training {len(pop.individuals)} models...\", flush=True)\n    83→            self._train_population(pop, X, y)\n    84→            self.horizon_models[horizon] = pop\n    85→            print(f\"    Completed horizon {horizon}\", flush=True)\n    86→\n    87→        self.is_fitted = True\n    88→        print(\"All horizon ensembles fitted\", flush=True)\n    89→\n    90→    def _train_population(self, population: Population, X: pd.DataFrame, y: pd.Series):\n    91→        \"\"\"Fit all models in a population.\"\"\"\n    92→        total = len(population.individuals)\n    93→        for i, ind in enumerate(population.individuals):\n    94→            try:\n    95→                print(f\"[horizon]   Training model {i+1}/{total} ({ind.model_type})...\", flush=True)\n    96→                ind.model.fit(X, y)\n    97→                print(f\"[horizon]   Model {i+1} trained\", flush=True)\n    98→            except Exception as e:\n    99→                print(f\"[horizon]   Model {i+1} failed: {e}\", flush=True)\n   100→                # Combined transaction cost: fee + slippage\n        entry_cost = self.fee_rate + self.slippage\n        exit_cost = self.fee_rate + self.slippage\n\n        # Determine if we have high/low for stop-loss\n        use_stop = self.stop_loss_pct > 0\n        if isinstance(prices, pd.DataFrame):\n            # Expect columns: 'close', optionally 'high', 'low'\n            if 'high' in prices.columns and 'low' in prices.columns:\n                close_series = prices['close']\n                high_series = prices['high']\n                low_series = prices['low']\n            else:\n                close_series = prices['close']\n                high_series = low_series = close_series\n        else:\n            close_series = prices\n            high_series = low_series = prices\n\n        # Align signals and prices\n        signals = signals.reindex(close_series.index).fillna(-1)\n\n        # Build equity curve indexed by signals.index\n        equity = pd.Series(index=signals.index, dtype=float)\n        equity.iloc[0] = capital\n\n        # Iterate through each timestamp, use signal to open a trade that closes at next timestamp\n        for i in range(len(signals) - 1):\n            sig = signals.iloc[i]\n            current_price = close_series.iloc[i]\n            next_close = close_series.iloc[i+1]\n            next_high = high_series.iloc[i+1]\n            next_low = low_series.iloc[i+1]\n\n            if sig == -1:\n                # No trade, carry forward capital\n                equity.iloc[i+1] = capital\n                continue\n\n            # Determine entry price with cost\n            if sig == 1:  # long\n                entry = current_price * (1 + entry_cost)\n                # Determine exit price considering stop-loss\n                stop_price = entry * (1 - self.stop_loss_pct) if use_stop else None\n                exit_price = next_close * (1 - exit_cost)\n                if use_stop and next_low <= stop_price:\n                    # Stop triggered: exit at stop price (with exit cost)\n                    exit_price = stop_price * (1 - exit_cost)\n                ret = (exit_price / entry) - 1\n            else:  # short\n                entry = current_price * (1 - entry_cost)\n                stop_price = entry * (1 + self.stop_loss_pct) if use_stop else None\n                exit_price = next_close * (1 + exit_cost)\n                if use_stop and next_high >= stop_price:\n                    exit_price = stop_price * (1 + exit_cost)\n                ret = (entry / exit_price) - 1\n\n            # Apply bet size\n            capital *= (1 + ret * self.bet_size)\n\n            self.trades.append({\n                \"entry_time\": signals.index[i],\n                \"exit_time\": signals.index[i+1],\n                \"entry_price\": entry,\n                \"exit_price\": exit_price,\n                \"return\": ret,\n                \"pnl\": capital - self.initial_capital,\n                \"stopped\": use_stop and ((sig == 1 and next_low <= stop_price) or (sig == 0 and next_high >= stop_price))\n            })\n\n            equity.iloc[i+1] = capital\n\n        # Bets per month (entries)\n        n_entries = len(self.trades)\n        if self.equity_curve is not None and len(self.equity_curve) > 0:\n            period_days = len(self.equity_curve) / (24 * 4)  # 15-min candles to days\n        else:\n            period_days = 0\n        months = period_days / 30.44\n        bets_per_month = n_entries / months if months > 0 else 0\n\n        # Sharpe\n        if self.equity_curve is not None:\n            eq_returns = self.equity_curve.pct_change().dropna()\n            if eq_returns.std() > 0:\n                sharpe = (eq_returns.mean() / eq_returns.std()) * np.sqrt(365 * 24 * 4)\n            else:\n                sharpe = 0.0\n\n            # Max drawdown\n            running_max = self.equity_curve.expanding().max()\n            drawdown = (self.equity_curve - running_max) / running_max\n            max_drawdown = abs(drawdown.min())\n        else:\n            sharpe = 0.0\n            max_drawdown = 0.0\n\n        total_return = (self.equity_curve.iloc[-1] - self.initial_capital) / self.initial_capital\n\n        gross_profit = sum(r for r in returns if r > 0)\n        gross_loss = abs(sum(r for r in returns if r < 0))\n        profit_factor = gross_profit / (gross_loss + 1e-10)\n\n        return {\n            \"accuracy\": accuracy,\n            \"bets_per_month\": bets_per_month,\n            \"sharpe\": sharpe,\n            \"max_drawdown\": max_drawdown,\n            \"total_return\": total_return,\n            \"n_trades\": len(self.trades),\n            \"profit_factor\": profit_factor,\n            \"final_equity\": self.equity_curve.iloc[-1] if self.equity_curve is not None else self.initial_capital,\n            \"gross_profit\": gross_profit,\n            \"gross_loss\": gross_loss\n        }\n\n    def get_equity_curve(self) -> pd.Series:\n        return self.equity_curve\n\n    def get_trades(self) -> pd.DataFrame:\n        return pd.DataFrame(self.trades)\n","numLines":204,"startLine":1,"totalLines":204}}}

    Run walk-forward validation with a single temporal split.\n        Train on data before the validation period, test on the most recent validation period.\n        This provides an honest OOS However, capping losses is crucial to prevent large drawdowns.\n\nActually, to improve Sharpe, we need to either:\n- Increase average win relative to average loss\n- Increase win rate\n- Reduce volatility of returns\n\nThe simulator's return calculation uses a fixed bet size. If we reduce bet size, the absolute PnL per trade scales down proportionally, but the ratio of win to loss remains the same. So if we have:\n- Average win: +0.062% (from Step 19)\n- Average loss: -1.0%\n- Win rate: ~84% (108 trades, ~91 wins)\n\n\nWin expectancy = (0.84 * 0.00062) + (0.16 * -0.01) = 0.0005208 - 0.0016 = -0.0010792 (negative)\n\nReducing position size proportionally reduces both gains and losses, but the negative expectancy remains. The Sharpe ratio might improve slightly because the volatility of equity curve would be lower (smaller bets), but the negative mean would still produce negative total return over many trades. However, the Step 19 results showed total return -2.26% with a large number of trades (469 per month). That's a small negative return overall, but the huge number of trades amplified the small negative expectancy.\n\nIf we reduce position size to 0.05, total return would be scaled down by factor 0.05/0.2 = 0.25. So -2.26% * 0.25 = -0.565% for the same number of trades. But the Sharpe is based on equity curve returns. The equity curve would have smaller fluctuations, potentially reducing volatility more than mean, so Sharpe might improve if the mean scales linearly but volatility scales less than linearly? Actually, if we reduce bet size, each trade's return is multiplied by the bet size factor. The equity curve becomes: capital_{t+1} = capital_t * (1 + bet_size * r_t). For small bet sizes, the returns approximately add: log returns approx bet_size * r_t. The mean of equity curve pct changes is approx bet_size * mean(r). The std is approx bet_size * std(r). So Sharpe (annualized) is approx (bet_size * mean(r) / (bet_size * std(r))) * sqrt(periods) = mean(r)/std(r) * sqrt(periods). That is independent of bet_size! So scaling bet size shouldn't change Sharpe much if the scaling is constant and returns are i.i.d. However, the formula in the simulator: `capital *= (1 + ret * self.bet_size)` is multiplicative, and the Sharpe calculation uses pct changes of the equity curve. For constant bet_size, the equity curve is geometric Brownian motion with returns = bet_size * r. Indeed, the Sharpe ratio scales as sqrt(T) * mean(bet_size * r) / std(bet_size * r) = sqrt(T) * mean(r) / std(r) (since bet_size cancels). So Sharpe should be roughly independent of bet_size if we ignore compounding effects and if the distribution of r is stable. But the actual observed Sharpe might change because of path dependency and larger bet sizes causing larger drawdowns that affect the mean and std differently? Actually, with constant bet_size, the sequence of multipliers is (1 + b*r_i). The log equity is sum(log(1 + b*r_i)). For small b, log(1+br) ≈ br - (br)^2/2. The mean log return ≈ b*mean(r) - b^2*var(r)/2. The variance of log returns ≈ b^2 * var(r). So the Sharpe (based on arithmetic returns) is (mean(1+br)-1)/std(1+br) = b*mean(r)/ (b*std(r)) = mean(r)/std(r). So it cancels exactly if we consider arithmetic returns. However, the equity curve's arithmetic returns are not exactly b*r because of compounding: each step's return depends on previous capital. But if b is small and returns are not huge, compounding is minor. So Sharpe should be relatively invariant to position size.\n\nBut Step 19 showed Sharpe -30.59, which is extremely negative. That's not because of bet size alone; it's because the model's predictions have negative expectancy (mean(r) negative). The large number of trades with negative mean leads to a steadily declining equity curve, giving negative Sharpe.\n\nTo improve Sharpe, we need to fix the negative expectancy, not just reduce bet size. Reducing bet size would reduce the total dollar loss but not change Sharpe much. However, it would reduce max drawdown percentage because the drawdown is proportional to bet size. But Sharpe might remain similar.\n\nThe plan mentioned \"Sharpe filtering\" in the initial description. In `run_walk_forward`, they rescore individuals on validation using Sharpe (line 301). So the selection pressure is on Sharpe. But the final consensus uses the top models, which are selected by Sharpe. So why is the final Sharpe so negative? Because the simulator used for final consensus is the same as for rescoring (line 320). So if the best models by Sharpe produce negative Sharpe on validation, that means the Sharpe itself is negative for those models.\n\nMaybe the issue is that the training/validation split leads to overfitting, and the Sharpe calculated on validation is negative but the models still get selected because they are the least negative? Or the population fitness on training is positive (based on accuracy), and the rescoring on validation uses Sharpe, but if all models have negative Sharpe, the best (least negative) is chosen, still negative.\n\nSo we need to either:\n- Improve model quality so that the true Sharpe is positive\n- Or add risk management that changes the Sharpe calculation (e.g., stop-loss) to make it more positive\n\nThe stop-loss could improve Sharpe by cutting losses short, turning large losses into smaller ones, thereby increasing mean(r) and reducing vol. For example, if we have an average loss of -1% and we cut it to -0.5% via stop-loss, then new expectancy becomes 0.84*0.00062 + 0.16*(-0.005) = 0.0005208 - 0.0008 = -0.0002792, still negative but less so. If we also reduce the win slightly because stops may exit winning positions? Actually stop-loss only triggers on adverse moves, not on winning. So wins remain the same. So we need a stop-loss level that catches enough of the large losses without being too tight.\n\nAlternatively, we could use position sizing based on recent volatility: bet smaller when volatility is high (when large losses are more likely). The simulator uses a constant bet_size per trade. But we could modify it to have dynamic bet_size. However, that would require passing a series of bet sizes or modifying the capital update logic.\n\nBut we might not need to implement ATR-based sizing right away if we use a stop-loss. Let's check the simulator's stop-loss logic: it uses `stop_loss_pct` relative to entry price (including costs). It checks if the next period's high/low touches the stop. That's a simple fixed percentage stop.\n\nGiven the problem as described, I think the immediate actions from Step 20 plan should be:\n\n1. **Fix horizon ensemble training bug** – already seems fixed, but I should verify that it's being called correctly and not causing NaNs. In `train_best_models`, it calls `self.horizon_ensemble.fit_horizon_models(horizon_data, y_recent)` at line 389. The second argument is `y_recent`, but the method signature `fit_horizon_models(self, horizon_data, target_series=None)` says target_series is ignored. So it's fine.\n\n2. **Introduce volatility-aware position sizing & stop-loss** – easiest: set a reasonable stop_loss_pct and maybe reduce position size. Let's set:\n   - POSITION_SIZE = 0.1 (10%) – a moderate reduction\n   - STOP_LOSS_PCT = 0.015 (1.5%) – tight enough to cut large losses\n\nBut we need to ensure that these are configurable and can be adjusted later.\n\n3. **Refine consensus thresholds** – Already, `adjust_thresholds` is called after walk-forward (line 471). That's good. But we should check what `adjust_thresholds` does to ensure it's effective.\n\nLet me read the consensus gate:","signature":""}],"model":"stepfun/step-3.5-flash:free","stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"output_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":null,"cache_read_input_tokens":null,"cache_creation":null,"inference_geo":null,"server_tool_use":null,"service_tier":null},"provider":"StepFun","context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"968cc0ec-4ed6-4a9c-b1cc-955169411baf","uuid":"4c46d257-3401-487b-b7fe-58c18fa9387b"}

At least MIN_MODELS_AGREE models must agree on direction\n    18→    - Average confidence must exceed MIN_CONFIDENCE\n    19→    \"\"\"\n    20→\n    21→    def __init__(\n    22→        self,\n    23→        min_models_agree: int = ConsensusConfig.MIN_MODELS_AGREE,\n    24→        min_confidence: float = ConsensusConfig.MIN_CONFIDENCE\n    25→    ):\n    26→        self.min_models_agree = min_models_agree\n    27→        self.min_confidence = min_confidence\n    28→\n    29→    def decide(\n    30→        self,\n    31→        models: List[Individual],\n    32→        X: pd.DataFrame\n    33→    ) -> pd.Series:\n    34→        \"\"\"\n    35→        Generate final trading signals (UP=1, DOWN=0, NO_TRADE=-1).\n    36→\n    37→        Args:\n    38→            models: list of trained model individuals\n    39→            X: feature DataFrame to predict on\n    40→\n    41→        Returns:\n    42→            Series of signals (1, 0, or -1) aligned to X.index\n    43→        \"\"\"\n    44→        signals = pd.Series(index=X.index, data=0)\n    45→        probas_matrix = []\n    46→\n    47→        for ind in models:\n    48→            try:\n    49→                proba = ind.model.predict_proba(X)\n    50→                probas_matrix.append(proba)\n    51→            except Exception as e:\n    52→                continue\n    53→\n    54→        if not probas_matrix:\n    55→            # No model worked, all NO_TRADE\n    56→            signals[:] = -1\n    57→            return signals\n    58→\n    59→        probas_array = np.array(probas_matrix)  # shape: (n_models, n_samples)\n    60→\n    61→        # Average confidence for each sample\n    62→        avg_proba = probas_array.mean(axis=0)\n    63→\n    64→        # Count models predicting UP\n    65→        up_votes = (probas_array >= 0.5).sum(axis=0)\n    66→\n    67→        down_votes = len(probas_matrix) - At least MIN_MODELS_AGREE models must agree on direction\n    - Average confidence must exceed MIN_CONFIDENCE\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        min_models_agree: int = ConsensusConfig.MIN_MODELS_AGREE,\n        min_confidence: float = ConsensusConfig.MIN_CONFIDENCE\n    ):\n        self.min_models_agree = min_models_agree\n        self.min_confidence = min_confidence\n\n    def decide(\n        self,\n        models: List[Individual],\n        X: pd.DataFrame\n    ) -> pd.Series:\n        \"\"\"\n        Generate final trading signals (UP=1, DOWN=0, NO_TRADE=-1).\n\n        Args:\n            models: list of trained model individuals\n            X: feature DataFrame to predict on\n\n        Returns:\n            Series of signals (1, 0, or -1) aligned to X.index\n        \"\"\"\n        signals = pd.Series(index=X.index, data=0)\n        probas_matrix = []\n\n        for ind in models:\n            try:\n                proba = ind.model.predict_proba(X)\n                probas_matrix.append(proba)\n            except Exception as e:\n                continue\n\n        if not probas_matrix:\n            # No model worked, all NO_TRADE\n            signals[:] = -1\n            return signals\n\n        probas_array = np.array(probas_matrix)  # shape: (n_models, n_samples)\n\n        # Average confidence for each sample\n        avg_proba = probas_array.mean(axis=0)\n\n        # Count models predicting UP\n        up_votes = (probas_array >= 0.5).sum(axis=0)\n\n        down_votes = len(probas_matrix) - up_votes\n\n        # Apply gating rules\n        for i, (avg_p, up, down) in enumerate(zip(avg_proba, up_votes, down_votes)):\n            # Check agreement\n            if up >= self.min_models_agree:\n                direction = 1\n                confidence = avg_p\n            elif down >= self.min_models_agree:\n                direction = 0\n                confidence = 1 - avg_p  # confidence in DOWN is 1 - avg_proba\n            else:\n                signals.iloc[i] = -1\n                continue\n\n            # Check confidence threshold\n            if confidence >= self.min_confidence:\n                signals.iloc[i] = direction\n            else:\n                signals.iloc[i] = -1\n\n        return signals\n\n    def adjust_thresholds(\n        self,\n        recent_performance: Dict[str, float],\n        target_accuracy: float = 0.65,\n        target_bets: float = 90.0\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Dynamically adjust consensus thresholds based on recent performance.\n\n        If accuracy is high but bet count too low: lower min_models_agree or min_confidence\n        If accuracy is low: raise thresholds\n        \"\"\"\n        accuracy = recent_performance.get(\"accuracy\", 0.5)\n        bets_per_month = recent_performance.get(\"bets_per_month\", 0.0)\n\n        if accuracy >= target_accuracy and bets_per_month < target_bets:\n            # Too strict, loosen\n            self.min_models_agree = max(1, self.min_models_agree - 1)\n            self.min_confidence = max(0.5, self.min_confidence - 0.02)\n        elif accuracy < target_accuracy:\n            # Too loose, tighten\n            self.min_models_agree = min(5, self.min_models_agree + 1)\n            self.min_confidence = min(0.8, self.min_confidence + 0.02)\n\n        # Clamp to reasonable ranges\n        self.min_models_agree = max(1, min(5, self.min_models_agree))\n        self.min_confidence = max(0.5, min(0.9, self.min_confidence))\n\n    def get_params(self) -> dict:\n        return {\n            \"min_models_agree\": self.min_models_agree,\n            \"min_confidence\": self.min_confidence\n        }\n","numLines":123,"startLine":1,"totalLines":123}}}

Select feature columns to carry forward (exclude raw price/volume and target/leakage)\n        exclude_cols = [\n            \"open_time\", \"open\", \"high\", \"low\", \"close\", \"volume\",\n            \"quote_volume\", \"trades_count\", \"target\", \"future_close\"\n        ]\n        feature_cols = [\n            col for col in source_df.columns\n            if col not in exclude_cols\n        ]\n\n        # Rename with horizon suffix (except base)\n        if name != \"15m\":\n            renamed = {col: f\"{col}_{name}\" for col in feature_cols}\n            source_df = source_df.rename(columns=renamed)\n            # Update feature_cols to use new names\n            feature_cols = [f\"{col}_{name}\" for col in feature_cols]\n\n        # Merge into result on open_time (may need forward fill to align to 15m)\n        print(f\"[horizon] Merging {len(feature_cols)} features for horizon {name}...\", flush=True)\n        to_merge = source_df[[\"open_time\"] + feature_cols].copy()\n        result_df = result_df.merge(to_merge, on=\"open_time\", how=\"left\")\n        print(f\"[horizon]   Merged (result now has {len(result_df)} rows, {len(result_df.columns)} cols)\", flush=True)\n\n    # Forward fill horizon features so they align with 15m timestamps\n    print(\"[horizon] Forward filling missing values...\", flush=True)\n    result_df = result_df.ffill()\n    print(f\"[horizon] Feature generation complete: {len(result_df)} rows, {len(result_df.columns)} columns\", flush=True)\n\n    return result_df\n","numLines":123,"startLine":1,"totalLines":123}}}

But I'll implement a simple rule-based.\n\nSpecifically:\n\n```\ndef adjust_thresholds(self, metrics):\n    sharpe = metrics.get('sharpe', -1000)\n    profit_factor = metrics.get('profit_factor', 0)\n    accuracy = metrics.get('accuracy', 0.5)\n    bets = metrics.get('bets_per_month', 0)\n    # Targets from overall goals:\n    TARGET_SHARPE = 1.0\n    TARGET_PROFIT_FACTOR = 1.2\n    TARGET_ACCURACY = 0.65\n    TARGET_BETS = 90.0\n\n    # If Sharpe or profit factor are below target, tighten significantly\n    if sharpe < TARGET_SHARPE or profit_factor < TARGET_PROFIT_FACTOR:\n        self.min_confidence = min(0.9, self.min_confidence + 0.05)\n        self.min_models_agree = min(5, self.min_models_agree + 1)\n    # If accuracy below target, tighten a bit\n    elif accuracy < TARGET_ACCURACY:\n        self.min_confidence = min(0.9, self.min_confidence + 0.03)\n    # If bets too low and accuracy decent, loosen\n    elif bets < TARGET_BETS and accuracy >= TARGET_ACCURACY:\n        self.min_confidence = max(0.5, self.min_confidence - 0.02)\n        self.min_models_agree = max(1, self.min_models_agree - 1)\n    # Else keep steady\n    # Clamp\n    self.min_confidence = max(0.5, min(0.95, self.min_confidence))\n    self.min_models_agree = max(1, min(5, self.min_models_agree))\n```\n\nThat should adapt thresholds to improve quality when Sharpe is low.\n\nBut we also need to consider that if we tighten too much, we might get zero trades. Primary: Sharpe and profitability\n        if sharpe < target_sharpe or profit_factor < target_profit_factor:\n            # Poor risk-adjusted/absolute performance: tighten to filter trades\n            self.min_confidence = min(0.9, self.min_confidence + 0.05)\n            self.min_models_agree = min(5, self.min_models_agree + 1)\n        elif accuracy < target_accuracy:\n            # Directional accuracy insufficient: tighten to require stronger agreement\n            self.min_confidence = min(0.9, self.min_confidence + 0.03)\n        elif bets_per_month < target_bets and accuracy >= target_accuracy:\n            # No model worked, all NO_TRADE\n            signals[:] = -1\n            return signals\n\n        probas_array = np.array(probas_matrix)  # shape: (n_models, n_samples)\n\n        # Average confidence for each sample\n        avg_proba = probas_array.mean(axis=0)\n\n        # Count models predicting UP\n        up_votes = (probas_array >= 0.5).sum(axis=0)\n\n        down_votes = len(probas_matrix) - up_votes\n\n        # Apply gating rules\n        for i, (avg_p, up, down) in enumerate(zip(avg_proba, up_votes, down_votes)):\n            # Check agreement\n            if up >= self.min_models_agree:\n                direction = 1\n                confidence = avg_p\n            elif down >= self.min_models_agree:\n                direction = 0\n                confidence = 1 - avg_p  # confidence in DOWN is 1 - avg_proba\n            else:\n                signals.iloc[i] = -1\n                continue\n\n            # Check confidence threshold\n            if confidence >= self.min_confidence:\n                signals.iloc[i] = direction\n            else:\n                signals.iloc[i] = -1\n\n        return signals\n\n    def adjust_thresholds(\n        self,\n        recent_performance: Dict[str, float],\n        target_accuracy: float = 0.65,\n        target_bets: float = 90.0\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Dynamically adjust consensus thresholds based on recent performance.\n\n        If accuracy is high but bet count too low: lower min_models_agree or min_confidence\n        If accuracy is low: raise thresholds\n        \"\"\"\n        accuracy = recent_performance.get(\"accuracy\", 0.5)\n        bets_per_month = recent_performance.get(\"bets_per_month\", 0.0)\n\n        if accuracy >= target_accuracy and bets_per_month < target_bets:\n            # Too strict, loosen\n            self.min_models_agree = max(1, self.min_models_agree - 1)\n            self.min_confidence = max(0.5, self.min_confidence - 0.02)\n        elif accuracy < target_accuracy:\n            # Too loose, tighten\n            self.min_models_agree = min(5, self.min_models_agree + 1)\n            self.min_confidence = min(0.8, self.min_confidence + 0.02)\n\n        # Clamp to reasonable ranges\n        self.min_models_agree = max(1, min(5, self.min_models_agree))\n        self.min_confidence = max(0.5, min(0.9, self.min_confidence))\n\n    def get_params(self) -> dict:\n        return {\n            \"min_models_agree\": self.min_models_agree,\n            \"min_confidence\": self.min_confidence\n        }\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":90,"oldLines":30,"newStart":90,"newLines":41,"lines":["     def adjust_thresholds(","         self,","         recent_performance: Dict[str, float],","+        target_sharpe: float = 1.0,","+        target_profit_factor: float = 1.2,","         target_accuracy: float = 0.65,","         target_bets: float = 90.0","     ):","         \"\"\"","         Dynamically adjust consensus thresholds based on recent performance."," ","-        If accuracy is high but bet count too low: lower min_models_agree or min_confidence","-        If accuracy is low: raise thresholds","+        Prioritizes risk-adjusted returns (Sharpe) and profitability (profit factor).","+        If Sharpe or profit factor are below target, tighten thresholds to improve quality.","+        If accuracy is high but Sharpe is low, also tighten (filter out low-quality trades).","+        If bets are too low and accuracy acceptable, loosen to increase frequency.","         \"\"\"","+        sharpe = recent_performance.get(\"sharpe\", -1000.0)","+        profit_factor = recent_performance.get(\"profit_factor\", 0.0)","         accuracy = recent_performance.get(\"accuracy\", 0.5)","         bets_per_month = recent_performance.get(\"bets_per_month\", 0.0)"," ","-        if accuracy >= target_accuracy and bets_per_month < target_bets:","-            # horizon -> population\n        self.main_features = []  # list of feature names produced by this ensemble\n        self.is_fitted = False\n\n    def fit_horizon_models(\n        self,\n        horizon_data: Dict[str, pd.DataFrame],\n        target_series: pd.Series = None\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Train a separate model population for each horizon.\n\n        Args:\n            horizon_data: dict of {horizon: DataFrame} with features and 'target' column for that horizon\n            target_series: ignored (for backward compatibility)\n        \"\"\"\n        self.horizon_models = {}\n\n        horizons = list(horizon_data.items())\n        print(f\"Fitting horizon ensembles for {len(horizons)} horizons\", flush=True)\n        for idx, (horizon, df) in enumerate(horizons):\n            if df.empty:\n                print(f\"  Horizon {horizon}: empty, skipping\", flush=True)\n                continue\n\n            print(f\"  Horizon {horizon} ({idx+1}/{len(horizons)}): processing {len(df)} rows\", flush=True)\n\n            # Set index for alignment\n            df_indexed = df.set_index(\"open_time\")\n\n            # Use the horizon-specific target from df['target']\n            if 'target' not in df_indexed.columns:\n                print(f\"    WARNING: no 'target' column in horizon data; skipping\", flush=True)\n                continue\n            y = df_indexed['target']\n\n            # Prepare features (exclude time and price/volume and target)\n            exclude_cols = [\"open_time\", \"open\", \"high\", \"low\", \"close\", \"volume\", \"quote_volume\", \"target\", \"future_close\"]\n            feature_cols = [c for c in df_indexed.columns if c not in exclude_cols]\n            X = df_indexed[feature_cols]\n\n            # Drop rows where target is NaN\n            valid_idx = y.notna()\n            if not valid_idx.any():\n                print(f\"    WARNING: all targets NaN; skipping\", flush=True)\n                continue\n            X = X[valid_idx]\n            y = y[valid_idx]\n\n            print(f\"    Feature count: {len(feature_cols)}, training samples: {len(X)}\", flush=True)\n\n            # Create population (use only random_forest for speed and stability)\n            pop = Population(\n                population_size=5,  # small for horizon models\n                model_types=[\"random_forest\"],\n                elitism_count=1\n            )\n            pop.initialize(input_dim=len(feature_cols), feature_names=feature_cols)\n\n            # Quick training: fit all models\n            print(f\"    Training {len(pop.individuals)} models...\", flush=True)\n            self._train_population(pop, X, y)\n            self.horizon_models[horizon] = pop\n            print(f\"    Completed horizon {horizon}\", flush=True)\n\n        self.is_fitted = True\n        print(\"All horizon ensembles fitted\", flush=True)\n\n    def _train_population(self, population: Population, X: pd.DataFrame, y: pd.Series):\n        \"\"\"Fit all models in a population.\"\"\"\n        total = len(population.individuals)\n        for i, ind in enumerate(population.individuals):\n            try:\n                print(f\"[horizon]   Training model {i+1}/{total} ({ind.model_type})...\", flush=True)\n                ind.model.fit(X, y)\n                print(f\"[horizon]   Model {i+1} trained\", flush=True)\n            except Exception as e:\n                print(f\"[horizon]   Model {i+1} failed: {e}\", flush=True)\n                # Set very low fitness if model fails\n                ind.fitness = -1000.0\n\n    def generate_features(\n        self,\n        horizon_data: Dict[str, pd.DataFrame],\n        base_index: pd.DatetimeIndex\n    ) -> pd.DataFrame:\n        \"\"\"\n        Generate horizon ensemble features: predictions from each horizon's best model.\n\n        Returns:\n            DataFrame with columns like: h_1h_pred, h_1h_proba, h_4h_pred, ...\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self.is_fitted:\n            raise RuntimeError(\"HorizonEnsemble must be fitted first\")\n\n        features = pd.DataFrame(index=base_index)\n\n        for horizon, pop in self.horizon_models.items():\n            best = pop.get_best(1)[0]\n\n            # Get horizon data aligned to base index\n            df_h = horizon_data[horizon].set_index(\"open_time\")\n            X_h = df_h.reindex(base_index)\n\n            # Drop non-feature columns\n            feature_cols = [c for c in X_h.columns if c not in [\"open\", \"high\", \"low\", \"close\", \"volume\", \"quote_volume\"]]\n            X_h_features = X_h[feature_cols]\n\n            # Forward fill any missing features (from resampling gaps)\n            X_h_features = X_h_features.ffill()\n\n            # Generate predictions\n            try:\n                proba = best.model.predict_proba(X_h_features)\n                pred = best.model.predict(X_h_features, threshold=0.5)\n                features[f\"h_{horizon}_proba\"] = proba\n                features[f\"h_{horizon}_pred\"] = pred\n            except Exception as e:\n                # If prediction fails, fill with 0.5 (neutral)\n                features[f\"h_{horizon}_proba\"] = 0.5\n                features[f\"h_{horizon}_pred\"] = 0\n\n        self.main_features = list(features.columns)\n        return features\n\n    def get_feature_names(self) -> List[str]:\n        return self.main_features\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":68,"oldLines":6,"newStart":68,"newLines":14,"lines":["             X = X[valid_idx]","             y = y[valid_idx]"," ","+            # Target: >=65% accuracy, >90 bets/month, positive Sharpe.\n\n## Current Status: 📊 Step 19 Completed – High Accuracy, Negative Sharpe\n\n### Step 19 Configuration\n- **Population:** POPULATION_SIZE=3, MODEL_TYPES=[\"random_forest\"]\n- **RF hyperparameter variation:**\n  - n_estimators: [30, 50]\n  - max_depth: [6, 8]\n  - min_samples_leaf: [10, 15]\n- **Training data:** ONLINE_DATA_DAYS=90, MAX_TRAIN_SAMPLES=3000\n- **Validation:** TRAIN_DAYS=14, VALID_DAYS=7, MAX_WALK_FORWARD_DAYS=30\n- **Horizons:** {\"15m\":1, \"1h\":4, \"4h\":16} (multi-horizon technical features)\n- **Consensus:** MIN_MODELS_AGREE=2, MIN_CONFIDENCE=0.65\n\n### Step 19 Results\nRun: `results/20260318_082918`\n\n- **Validation accuracy:** 0.8426 (exceeds 65% target)\n- **Bets/month:** 469.65 (far exceeds 90 target)\n- **Sharpe:** -30.59 (deeply negative)\n- **Total return:** -2.26%\n- **Max drawdown:** 2.29%\n- **Profit factor:** 0.331 (gross profit 0.0565, gross loss 0.1707)\n- **Number of trades (validation):** 108\n- **Latest signal:** -1 (NO_TRADE)\n- **Population fitness:** best ~0.81 (training accuracy)\n\n### Step 19 Observations\n- **Paradox:** Accuracy is excellent (84%) but profitability is terrible (negative expectancy).\n- Trade distribution: 108 trades → ~91 wins (positive returns) and ~17 losses. However, average win ~0.062% while average loss ~1.0%. Losses are ~16× larger than wins → negative expectancy despite high win rate.\n- The simulator produced negative total return and very low profit factor (0.33), confirming that the model's correct predictions capture only tiny moves while incorrect predictions result in large adverse moves.\n- Horizon ensemble training failed with \"Input y contains NaN.\" errors due to misaligned target series. Horizon features (resampled technicals) are used by the base model, but horizon model predictions are not integrated yet.\n- Consensus gate with confidence=0.65 allowed many trades (469/mo), so frequency is not an issue.\n- Training fitness (~0.81) is high but validation Sharpe extremely negative, indicating overfitting to training regime or regime shift between training and validation.\n- Runtime ~1-2 min, acceptable.\n\n### Diagnosis – Why High Accuracy ≠ Profitability?\n1. **Asymmetric win/loss distribution:** Model predicts small bullish/bearish moves correctly most of the time, but when wrong, the market moves strongly against the position (e.g., strong one-sided moves). Without stops, a single large loss can wipe out many small gains.\n2. **Volatility-blind position sizing:** Fixed bet size (20% of capital) exposed to large losses during high volatility or gap moves.\n3. **No stop-loss:** The simulator holds for exactly one 15-minute period; if price moves sharply against within that period, the full loss is taken.\n4. **Potential overfitting:** Validation Sharpe suggests the trained models perform poorly OOS despite training accuracy, possibly due to regime change or data snooping.\n5. **Horizon ensemble integration broken:** The horizon model predictions are not used, missing potential cross-horizon confirmation that could improve risk-adjusted returns.\n6. **Target definition:** Predicting any directional move regardless of magnitude may lead to taking low-edge trades with tiny expected gains but occasional large losses.\n\n### Step 20 Plan – Risk-Aware Trading & Horizon Fix\n\nWe need to convert high accuracy into positive expectancy by managing risk and improving model quality.\n\n#### A. Fix Horizon Ensemble Training\n- Bug: `HorizonEnsemble.fit_horizon_models()` reindexes base target (15m) to horizon timestamps, causing NaNs. Should use the horizon-specific `target` column directly from the horizon DataFrame.\n- Modification: In `fit_horizon_models`, for each horizon, use `df['target']` after dropping NaNs, instead of reindexing external target_series.\n- This enables horizon models to be trained properly. Later we can consider using their predictions as features or in consensus.\n\n#### B. Introduce Volatility-Aware Position Sizing & Stop-Loss\n- Modify `SimulatedTrader` to support:\n  - Dynamic bet size based on recent volatility (e.g., ATR normalized) to reduce exposure during high volatility.\n  - Optional stop-loss: exit early if price moves against entry by X% (e.g., 1× ATR) before the fixed holding period.\n  - Alternatively, use a fixed fractional position sizing with a maximum per-trade risk cap.\n- Initially simpler: reduce `POSITION_SIZE` from 0.2 to 0.05 (5% of capital per trade) to limit drawdown. This alone can improve Sharpe if the model's edge is real but losses are amplified by sizing.\n- But better: compute position size as `min(bet_size, risk_capital / (entry_price * ATR))` for a risk-based approach.\n\n#### C. Refine Consensus Thresholds Based on Recent Performance\n- The `ConsensusGate.adjust_thresholds()` method exists but is not called automatically. Add a step after walk-forward to call `adjust_thresholds(metrics)` to adapt thresholds for the next iteration.\n- This helps tune between frequency and accuracy.\n\n#### D. Possibly Increase Diversity\n- If runtime allows, increase POPULATION_SIZE to 5 and extend hyperparameter ranges (e.g., max_depth up to 10, n_estimators up to 100) to search for more robust models.\n- But memory constraints previously caused OOM; monitor usage.\n\n#### E. Fitness Improvement\n- The population fitness already uses Sharpe during validation rescoring. That's good. We'll also log profit_factor and penalize low profit_factor.\n\n#### Step 20 Proposed Configuration (tentative)\n- Keep: POPULATION_SIZE=3, MODEL_TYPES=[\"random_forest\"], ONLINE_DATA_DAYS=90, MAX_TRAIN_SAMPLES=3000\n- Expand RF: max_depth ∈ [8, 10, 12], n_estimators ∈ [50, 100]\n- Validation: TRAIN_DAYS=14, VALID_DAYS=7 (keep)\n- Consensus: start with MIN_CONFIDENCE=0.65, MIN_MODELS_AGREE=2; call `adjust_thresholds()` based on previous metrics.\n- Position sizing: reduce POSITION_SIZE to 0.05 or implement ATR-based sizing.\n- Horizon: keep 1h and 4h; fix training bug.\n- Optionally add stop-loss (e.g., 2× ATR) in simulator.\n\n#### Targets\n- Accuracy ≥ 0.65\n- Bets/month ≥ 90\n- Sharpe > 1.0 (positive)\n- Profit factor > 1.2\n\nWe will implement these changes incrementally, starting with fixing horizon training and reducing position size to test if Sharpe improves.\n\n## Previous Critical Steps (for context)\n- **Step 14:** conf=0.65, depth=8, min_leaf=10, pop=5, max_train=4000 → accuracy 0.5517, bets 126.11/mo, Sharpe -27.37.\n- **Steps 15 & 16:** OOM kills.\n- **Step 17:** Timeout after 68m.\n- **Step 18:** Excessive confidence → zero trades.","newString":"# ArBos Trading System - State\n\n## Summary\nBTC 15-minute directional prediction system with evolutionary model search and walk-forward validation. Target: >=65% accuracy, >90 bets/month, positive Sharpe.\n\n## Current Status: 📈 Step 20 Completed – Risk Management Improves Drawdown, Profitability Still Negative\n\n### Step 20 Configuration\n- **Population:** POPULATION_SIZE=5, MODEL_TYPES=[\"random_forest\"]\n- **RF hyperparameter variation:**\n  - n_estimators: [50, 100]\n  - max_depth: [8, 10, 12]\n  - min_samples_leaf: [10, 15]\n- **Training data:** ONLINE_DATA_DAYS=90, MAX_TRAIN_SAMPLES=3000\n- **Validation:** TRAIN_DAYS=14, VALID_DAYS=7, MAX_WALK_FORWARD_DAYS=30\n- **Horizons:** {\"15m\":1, \"1h\":4, \"4h\":16} (multi-horizon technical features)\n- **Consensus:** MIN_MODELS_AGREE=2, MIN_CONFIDENCE=0.65\n- **Risk management:** POSITION_SIZE=0.05 (5% per trade), STOP_LOSS_PCT=0.015 (1.5% stop)\n- **Consensus adaptation:** adjust_thresholds() now considers Sharpe and profit factor in addition to accuracy and bet count\n\n### Step 20 Results\nRun: `results/20260318_084445`\n\n- **Validation accuracy:** 0.84 (exceeds 65% target)\n- **Bets/month:** 434.86 (far exceeds 90 target)\n- **Sharpe:** -27.52 (still deeply negative)\n- **Total return:** -0.44% (improved from -2.26%)\n- **Max drawdown:** 0.44% (improved from 2.29%)\n- **Profit factor:** 0.365 (gross profit 0.0503, gross loss 0.1378)\n- **Number of trades (validation):** 100\n- **Latest signal:** -1 (NO_TRADE)\n- **Population fitness:** best ~0.868\n\n### Step 20 Observations\n- **Risk management effective:** Reducing position size from 20% to 5% and adding 1.5% stop-loss dramatically reduced maximum drawdown and total loss magnitude (from -2.26% to -0.44% over 7 days).\n- **Horizon ensemble training:** Completed successfully without NaN errors. Both 1h and 4h horizon models trained on their respective resampled data.\n- **Consensus adaptation threshold update:** After walk-forward, `adjust_thresholds()` increased `MIN_CONFIDENCE` by 0.05 (to 0.70) and `MIN_MODELS_AGREE` by 1 (to 3) due to Sharpe < 1.0. This will make signal generation more selective in Step 21.\n- **Profitability still negative:** Despite improved risk control, profit factor remains below 0.4 and Sharpe is still negative (though magnitude may be smaller now due to reduced bet size). Gross profit sum of returns = 0.0503, gross loss = 0.1378 → net negative expectancy.\n- **Accuracy remains high:** 84% directional accuracy, indicating model skill but not translating to profits due to asymmetric returns (wins tiny, losses larger).\n- **Population diversity increased:** 5 individuals with expanded RF hyperparameters; best training fitness 0.868.\n\n### Diagnosis – Why Still Negative Expectancy?\n1. **Asymmetric returns persist:** Average win likely still around 0.06% of price, average loss ~0.8-1% after stop. Stop-loss reduced loss magnitude somewhat, but still losses outweigh many small wins.\n2. **Cost barrier:** Trading costs (fees + slippage = 0.15% round-trip) impose a ~0.3% hurdle per round-trip. Many winning trades may barely exceed costs, while losses exceed the stop occasionally.\n3. **Model confidence vs. magnitude:** High directional accuracy does not guarantee profitable returns if predicted moves are smaller than transaction costs or if incorrect predictions lead to moves several times larger than correct ones.\n4. **Thresholds still too permissive?** Even with 84% accuracy, the consensus may be allowing trades with confidence only slightly above 0.5, resulting in a low signal-to-noise ratio.\n5. **Horizon predictions not used as consensus voters:** Horizon models are only providing features; their own predictions might add independent confirmation but are not included in consensus voting.\n\n### Step 21 Plan – Tighten Quality Filter & Evaluate Hope\n\nThe next step should test whether stricter thresholds (now 3 models, 70% confidence) improve risk-adjusted returns by filtering out low-quality, low-conviction trades. Since we already have >400 bets/month, reducing frequency is acceptable to improve Sharpe.\n\n#### A. Run with Adjusted Thresholds\n- The consensus gate will now require at least 3 models agreeing and average confidence ≥ 0.70.\n- Expect reduced bet count (maybe < 200/month) but hopefully higher profit factor and Sharpe.\n\n#### B. Evaluate Impact\n- After Step 21 run, check if profit factor moves above 0.5 or 1.0, and whether Sharpe becomes less negative or positive.\n- Also analyze trade distribution: average win vs loss, and win rate.\n\n#### C. Consider Further Enhancements if Needed\nIf Sharpe remains deeply negative:\n- Increase `MIN_CONFIDENCE` further (e.g., to 0.75 or 0.80) to only take very high-conviction trades.\n- Increase `MIN_MODELS_AGREE` to 4 (with population 5, that's near-unanimity).\n- Implement ATR-based dynamic position sizing: scale bet size inversely with recent ATR to normalize risk.\n- Incorporate horizon model predictions into consensus (treat them as additional \"models\").\n- Adjust fitness to penalize low profit factor during validation rescoring (currently uses Sharpe; could incorporate profit factor directly).\n\n#### D. Horizon Ensemble as Additional Signals\n- Explore using horizon model predictions as extra consensus voters (e.g., include best horizon model predictions as votes alongside main models). This would require modifying ConsensusGate to accept additional model individuals.\n\n#### Targets for Step 21\n- Sharpe > 0 (positive)\n- Profit factor > 0.6\n- Maintain accuracy ≥ 0.6\n- Bets/month ≥ 150 (still above 90 but reduced from 400+)\n\n### Previous Critical Steps (for context)\n- **Step 14:** conf=0.65, depth=8, min_leaf=10, pop=5, max_train=4000 → accuracy 0.5517, bets 126.11/mo, Sharpe -27.37.\n- **Steps 15 & 16:** OOM kills.\n- **Step 17:** Timeout after 68m.\n- **Step 18:** Excessive confidence → zero trades.\n- **Step 19:** High accuracy (84%) but negative expectancy (Sharpe -30.6, profit factor 0.33, total return -2.26%).","originalFile":"# ArBos Trading System - State\n\n## Summary\nBTC 15-minute directional prediction system with evolutionary model search and walk-forward validation.
